# Tech Lead context

Technical memory: architecture, stack, decisions, gotchas. Append durable learnings
at the top of the relevant section, dated.

## Stack

- **Vite + TypeScript** (vanilla, no framework). Canvas-heavy rendering, so a UI
  framework adds little.
- **opensheetmusicdisplay (OSMD)** renders MusicXML to SVG and provides the sheet
  highlight cursor.
- **Tone.js** for synthesis (PolySynth) and the playback transport/clock.
- Canvas 2D for the falling notes and the piano keyboard.
- **Vitest** for unit tests.

## Architecture

- `src/main.ts` — glue: file load, OSMD setup, Tone.js scheduling, the rAF render loop,
  transport controls, and cursor sync.
- `src/score.ts` — `extractScore(osmd)` walks the score with a cloned iterator and
  converts each note's whole-note timestamp/length into absolute seconds. Returns
  `{ notes, stepTimes, duration }`.
- `src/visualizer.ts` — `Visualizer` class: piano layout, falling-note bars, active-key
  highlight. Pure rendering given a current time.
- `src/piano.ts` — 88-key geometry (MIDI 21..108), white/black key layout, name helpers.

**Sync invariant:** the falling notes and the sheet cursor are both driven from the same
note timestamps (`score.notes[i].time` and `score.stepTimes`). They cannot drift apart by
construction; tempo only changes playback speed, not sync.

## Decisions

- **2026-06-04 - BUGFIX (fix/fusion-rhythm-overread): an UNMATCHED geom chord took a blind QUARTER fallback that OVERFILLED its bar (reverie's last bar read 4.5 beats in 4/4).** Branch off main, not yet merged. CONFIRMED on the box (reverie eval fixture, `fusion._chords_by_cell` dump of the cached `reverie.geom.xml`/`.clarity.xml`): geom m17 staff1 = A4 + four shorts (C6 B5 C6 B5), all placeholder `duration:1`; Clarity read the same bar but ORDERED the four shorts C6 B5 **B5 C6** (vs geom's C6 B5 **C6 B5**), so geom's LAST short (B5) fails the pitch-class Needleman-Wunsch (`_nw`) and is UNMATCHED. The old fallback gave it a neutral quarter (dur16=4); the matched borrows already filled 8+2+2+2=14 of the 16-sixteenth bar, so the bar summed to **18 == 4.5 beats** (the user's symptom). Candidate #1 (use geom's OWN decoded duration) does NOT apply: the deployed geom is the notehead path (`transcribe_with_detector`), which fakes `duration:1` for EVERY note (verified: geom dur16 histogram is `{1: N}` on all 4 eval pieces); #196's symbol decode is research-only and not in the prod fusion path (`worker.geom_command` omits `--symbols`). `rhythm_repair` legitimately can't mask it (it skips the last bar AND refuses to shrink a pitched overfull bar by design).
  - **FIX = a capacity-clamped fallback (`omr-worker/fusion.py`).** New pure `_bar_capacity16(beats, beat_type)` (bar capacity in `omr_eval._dur16` SIXTEENTHS: `beats*16/beat_type`; 4/4->16, 2/4->8, 3/4/6/8->12; None on an odd meter) + `_bar_fallback_durs(durs, capacity16, fallback)`: a matched chord (an int) passes through unchanged; an UNMATCHED chord (a None) takes `clamp(room_remaining, 1, quarter)`, consuming the bar's leftover room greedily. A lone unmatched chord in a near-empty bar still gets a full quarter (room >= 4), so this is IDENTICAL to the old behaviour EXCEPT where a quarter would overfill (room < 4) -- exactly the over-read case. Floors at ONE sixteenth so every geom notehead keeps a positive duration (a dropped note would regress geom's pitch edge), even when the matched borrows already overfill. `capacity16=None` -> blind quarter (old behaviour). `_build` reads the NORMALIZED meter `fuse` already resolves (a 2/2 cut-time misread normalised to 4/4 -> cap 16), so the clamp matches the rendered meter. The clamp NEVER touches a borrowed (matched) duration, and pitch is geom's untouched, so it cannot regress pitch.
  - **MEASURED never-worse on the box (`fusion_repair_eval.py`, BEFORE deployed fusion vs AFTER via `RHY_SRC=/tmp/scratch_rhythm` shadowing the edited fusion).** reverie: m17 now sums to 16 (was 18); incomplete bars after repair **1/32 -> 0/32**; ndf1/dacc/nf1 unchanged 0.427/0.898/0.476 (the bar is RENDERED correct now; the metric is pitch-gated on geom's B5-vs-truth mismatch, so the duration change alone adds no exact (midi,dur16) match). tctab: FUSED note_dur_f1 **0.875 -> 0.890**, duration_acc **0.880 -> 0.894**, incomplete bars after repair **12/134 -> 6/134**, nf1 unchanged 0.995; overfull bars 12 -> 6. icarus + liminality: IDENTICAL (no unmatched chord lands in an overfull bar; clamp is a no-op). NO regression on any piece. The residual tctab overfull bars (e.g. m68 sum 26) are a DIFFERENT culprit -- Clarity's OWN over-read on the MATCHED side (every chord there is a borrowed duration, no unmatched fallback) -- which this fix deliberately does not touch.
  - **TESTS (`omr-worker/test_fusion.py`, +6; 26 fusion tests, full omr-worker suite 463 passed / 15 torch-skipped locally).** The reverie m17 shape (half + four shorts, one re-ordered -> unmatched, asserts bar sums to 16 not 18), the bar-already-full sixteenth floor, the non-4/4 (2/4) capacity, and a direct `_bar_fallback_durs` unit. The existing `test_fuse_unmatched_geom_chord_keeps_quarter_fallback` STILL passes unchanged (its unmatched note has room >= a quarter, so the clamp is a no-op there -- the surgical property).

- **2026-06-04 - BUGFIX (fix/edit-infer-type, uncommitted, SAME branch as the `<type>` fix): the docked edit toolbar `#edit-toolbar` (undo/redo + pitch + delete buttons) VANISHED from the DOM in edit mode on LARGE scores (reverie, 185 notes) while it persisted on the 15-note demo.** Root-caused in Chrome on reverie: `#edit-toolbar` was present on load + after OSMD render, but `document.getElementById('edit-toolbar')` returned null after entering edit mode, while `#verovio-host` (also inside `#sheet`) survived. CAUSE: `#edit-toolbar` was static markup nested INSIDE `<div id="sheet">`. OSMD owns `#sheet` and an `osmd.load`/render clears/detaches `#sheet`'s children. `renderVerovio` already RE-APPENDS `#verovio-host` for exactly this (`main.ts` ~659-663), but nothing re-attached the static toolbar; the module grabs it ONCE (`editToolbar` at `main.ts:127`) and only toggles `.hidden`. A large score's tall layout fires an autoResize OSMD re-render around enter-edit, which detaches `#edit-toolbar`, so `.hidden = false` then acted on a DETACHED node and the buttons never appeared. The small demo never triggers that re-render, so its toolbar survived, which is why every demo test passed (keyboard editing still worked via the window-level keydown handler, masking it further).
  - **FIX (`index.html` + `src/style.css`, NO `main.ts` change needed): move `#edit-toolbar` OUT of `#sheet` into a new `#sheet-pane` wrapper so OSMD can never touch it.** `#sheet-pane` is the flex slot in `#app`'s column that `#sheet` used to occupy: it now carries the pane HEIGHT (the 42%/34%@600px/30%@380px responsive heights moved from `#sheet` to `#sheet-pane`), is `position: relative`, and is `display:flex; flex-direction:column`. It stacks `#edit-toolbar` (`flex:0 0 auto`, in flow at the top, was `position:sticky;top:0` inside `#sheet`) above `#sheet` (`flex:1; min-height:0; overflow-y:auto`, scrolls beneath the docked strip). `#sheet` KEEPS `position:relative` (it is the offset parent for `#sheet-labels` and the runtime `#verovio-host`, both position children that scroll with its content). The module's `editToolbar` reference + `.hidden` show/hide now act on a node OSMD cannot detach, so it is reliable across ANY OSMD re-render (incl. a later autoResize while editing). Visually identical: docked brass strip at the top of the sheet pane, staff scrolls under it; edit-OFF is still a true no-op (`#edit-toolbar[hidden]` -> display:none, `#sheet` reclaims the full pane).
  - **SUBTLETY - the `#sheet:empty::before` empty-pane hint was DEAD and stays dead.** The "Load a MusicXML file..." hint never matched while the hidden `#edit-toolbar` was a child of `#sheet` (a hidden child still defeats `:empty`), so it has not shown on first load since Smart Edit landed. Moving the toolbar out would RESURRECT it (an unrequested visible change to the no-score state), so I re-scoped the rule to `#sheet-pane:empty::before`; `#sheet-pane` always has `#edit-toolbar` + `#sheet` children, so `:empty` never matches and the empty pane stays blank EXACTLY as today. Reviving the hint is a deliberate Designer call, not a side effect of this fix. Also dropped the now-dead `:not(#edit-toolbar)` from `#sheet.editing > *:not(#verovio-host)` (toolbar no longer a `#sheet` child).
  - **TEST:** `src/edit-toolbar-dom.test.ts` (NEW, `@vitest-environment jsdom`) parses the REAL `index.html` into a DOM and asserts the structural invariant directly: `sheet.contains(editToolbar) === false` (OSMD cannot detach it), `sheetPane.contains(editToolbar) === true` + `contains(sheet)`, toolbar docked before `#sheet` in the wrapper, starts `hidden`, and the whole button subtree (undo/redo/pitch/delete/add) rode along inside the relocated toolbar. GOTCHA for jsdom text-reading tests: `import.meta.url` is NOT a `file:` URL under the jsdom environment, so `fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)` throws "The URL must be of scheme file"; read the file via `join(process.cwd(), "index.html")` instead (the node-env text tests like `toolbar.test.ts` use `fileURLToPath` only because they run in the default node env). 526 tests green (was 519; +7), typecheck + build green, verovio WASM still code-splits out of `main`. Left in the worktree on the SAME branch as the `<type>` fix, NOT committed.

- **2026-06-04 - BUGFIX (fix/edit-infer-type, uncommitted): EDIT mode rendered the WRONG RHYTHM and click-to-select did NOTHING on real OMR scores, because the OMR omits `<type>`.** Reproduced live + in node (real Verovio) on the user's `reverie` (`src/test-fixtures/reverie-omr.musicxml`, a grand staff). Real OMR emits `<note><pitch>..</pitch><duration>2</duration><staff>1</staff></note>` with `<duration>` (in divisions) but NO `<type>` (and no `<voice>`). Verovio WITHOUT `<type>` draws EVERY note at a uniform default value (wrong rhythm) AND computes a wrong timemap; OSMD (the read-only view, edit OFF) infers the value from `<duration>` and renders right, which is why ONLY edit mode broke and every prior fixture (all carried `<type>`) missed it. Two symptoms, ONE cause: (1) notes lose duration; (2) click-to-select maps a clicked notehead to a VisNote by (midi, ONSET sec) - VisNote/model onsets come from `<duration>` (correct) but Verovio's onsets come from the wrong default durations, so they diverge after the first long note and `idToVisIndex.get(id)` returns undefined. MEASURED on reverie: before, `idToVisIndex` covered 23/185 notes and Verovio onsets diverged (`71@0.500` vs model `71@0.250`); after, 185/185 and onsets match exactly.
  - **FIX (`src/edit-model.ts`): infer + INSERT a `<type>` (plus `<dot>`s) during the parse walk, for every `<note>` AND `<rest>` that LACKS one.** New pure `noteTypeForDuration(durDivs, divisions)` -> `{type, dots}`: q = durDivs/divisions (quarters); match q against `base * {1, 1.5, 1.75}` (0/1/2 dots) over the standard bases longest-first (breve 8q .. 64th 0.0625q), preferring fewest dots + longest base (the conventional spelling); a non-standard duration (tuplet remainder, 0, divisions 0) falls back to the NEAREST base with 0 dots so it NEVER throws and Verovio always gets a valid value. `addTypeIfMissing(noteEl, durDivs, divisions)` is a strict NO-OP when the note already has a `<type>` (so demo/publisher/`<type>`-carrying scores are byte-for-byte untouched) and inserts in valid DTD order (`<type>` after `<duration>`/`<voice>`, before `<dot>`*/`<accidental>`/`<staff>`; `<dot>`s right after `<type>`). Called in `reindexHandles` right after `durDivs` is computed (`if (durDivs > 0)`), so it covers pitched notes, chord members, and rests. IDEMPOTENT: a structural edit re-runs `reindexHandles`, but the note now has a `<type>` so the 2nd pass is a no-op (no double-insert; tested with delete+restore). `serialize()` re-emits the mutated DOM, so Verovio receives `<type>` and produces the right rhythm + a correct timemap, which restores BOTH symptoms. The model's own onset math (from `<duration>`) is unchanged; pitch/delete/add/undo-redo/dual-surface-sync/edit-off-no-op all intact. The model is built + serialized ONLY in edit mode (`main.ts` 553 `enterEditMode`, serialize only feeds `renderMusicXml` at 666/2544), so the read-only OSMD path is untouched.
  - **TESTS + the gate prior work missed (verify on the REAL no-`<type>` file, not just `<type>`-carrying fixtures).** `edit-model-integration.test.ts` loads the REAL reverie through REAL Verovio and proves BEFORE/AFTER: rendering the RAW file gives divergent onsets + `idToVisIndex < notes/2`; rendering the model-serialized (fixed) XML gives onsets that EQUAL the model's + a COMPLETE map (every notehead clickable), plus per-note onset agreement and the inferred-type assertions (duration 2 -> eighth, 16 -> whole, 12-rest -> dotted half). `edit-model.test.ts` pins `noteTypeForDuration` (plain, dotted, double-dotted, longest-base/fewest-dots tie-break, nearest-base fallback, no-throw) + the no-`<type>` synthetic grand-staff fixture (`src/test-fixtures/no-type-grand-staff.musicxml`: half+quarters+whole+dotted-half+quarter-rest) for type insertion, valid child order, true onsets, the typed-score no-op, and idempotency. 519 tests green (was 506; +13), typecheck + build green, verovio WASM still code-splits out of `main`. Left in the worktree, NOT committed.

- **2026-06-04 - REVIEW-GATE (fix/edit-staff-readability @ d90e931): SHIP, no blocking findings.** Verified the `pageWidth` math (`round(max(320,w)*100/VEROVIO_SCALE)` at scale 50) makes `pageWidth*scale/100 == container` exactly (Math.round is exact for w=1500 -> pw 3000 -> 1500px), so the CSS `max-width:100%` (`src/style.css` #verovio-host svg) is a no-op and never downscales; all three render paths (`renderMusicXml`, `renderVerovio`, `renderVerovioPreview`) and the debounced resize handler recompute width from `sheetContainer.clientWidth` fresh, and `#sheet{overflow-y:auto}` + SVG `height:auto` + `breaks:"auto"`/`pageHeight 60000`/`adjustPageHeight` scroll multi-system scores without clipping. Hit-zone: `nearestNoteGWithinPadding`'s `isMapped` predicate (idToVisIndex -> visIndexToHandle.has) is byte-identical to the direct-hit handle resolution, so a padded notehead always maps (handle can only be undefined on a DIRECT hit = the documented tie-continuation no-op); noteheads resolve before rests in the pointerdown, so a tap near both wins the note. `REST_HIT_PADDING`->`GLYPH_HIT_PADDING` rename has zero dangling refs (Grep clean); both padded helpers keep the old `(clientX,clientY)` signature with one call site each, so rest selection is unchanged. Diff is confined to `buildToolkitOptions` + the two pointerdown helpers + the pure `nearestPaddedBoxIndex`; pitch/delete/add/undo-redo/dual-surface-sync/edit-off-no-op untouched. `buildToolkitOptions`/`VEROVIO_SCALE` have no external consumers. 506 tests green, typecheck + build green, verovio WASM still code-splits out of `main`. Non-blocking nit only: the >=24px padded hot zone can let a near-miss select a notehead whose bbox the tap is not inside (intended; the readability/finger-target goal), and on a dense chord two padded zones can overlap (nearest-center tie-break handles it). No fix needed.

- **2026-06-04 - BUGFIX (fix/edit-staff-readability, uncommitted): the edit-mode Verovio staff rendered as a tiny ~200px strip (unreadable) and noteheads were near-impossible to tap.** Both traced to ONE option bug in `buildToolkitOptions` (`src/verovio-view.ts`). Verovio's rendered SVG px width = `pageWidth * scale / 100` (pageWidth is 1/100 mm). The old options set `pageWidth = containerWidth * 5` at `scale 40`, so for a 1500px pane the SVG was ~3000px wide. The CSS sizes the host SVG with `max-width: 100%`, so the browser then SHRANK the whole 3000px engraving (glyphs and all) ~0.5x to fit, halving notehead size; with `breaks: "auto"` a short score also stayed on ONE system, so the strip read tiny. Measured the real toolkit in node to confirm (3000px SVG at scale40/pw=w*5). FIX: derive `pageWidth = containerWidthPx * 100 / scale` so the intrinsic px width EQUALS the container (CSS never downscales), and raise the engraving to `scale 50` (exported as `VEROVIO_SCALE`). At scale 50 the staff space renders ~9px and a notehead ~10px (measured) - comparable to OSMD's default and ~2.5x the old effective size. Long scores now wrap into multiple systems that scroll in #sheet (`pageHeight 60000`, `adjustPageHeight`). Trimmed page margins (50) for edge-to-edge like OSMD. Floor container at 320px so a hidden/unmeasured pane never lays out at width 0.
  - **Notehead tap was unforgiving (required a DIRECT g.note hit, ~10px target).** Generalized the rest hot-zone to noteheads: extracted the pure geometry into `nearestPaddedBoxIndex(boxes, x, y, padding)` in `verovio-view.ts` (unit-tested, no DOM), and main.ts now has one shared `nearestMappedGWithinPadding(selector, isMapped, x, y)` DOM helper that both `nearestNoteGWithinPadding` and `nearestRestGWithinPadding` call. The staff pointerdown tries a direct g.note hit first (fast path), else the nearest mapped notehead within a 12px-each-side (>=24px) zone; noteheads resolve before rests so a tap near both selects the note. `REST_HIT_PADDING` (12) renamed to the shared `GLYPH_HIT_PADDING`. A notehead that maps to no handle (tie continuation) is skipped in `isMapped` so it never wins the padded match. Pitch/delete/add/undo-redo/dual-surface-sync untouched.
  - **TESTS:** `verovio-view.test.ts` +11: `nearestPaddedBoxIndex` (direct hit, near-miss within pad, beyond pad = null, nearest-center tie-break, >=24px-zone goal) and `buildToolkitOptions` (pageWidth*scale/100 == container, scale >= 40, 0-width floor to 320, auto breaks + tall page). 506 tests green (was 495), typecheck + build green. Verify in a browser: the engraving should fill the pane width and read like the OSMD view, and a tap on or NEAR a notehead should select it.

- **2026-06-04 - REVIEW-GATE FIX (feat/edit-add, on top of 05cfc7a): the absolute-onset measure-advance also under-counted a trailing `<forward>`.** The new `reindexHandles` accumulated `measureMaxCursor` only on notes/rests, so a measure whose furthest cursor was reached by a trailing `<backup>`/`<forward>` (a voice that rests out the bar end as a `<forward>` instead of an explicit `<rest>`) advanced the absolute clock too little, breaking onsets (and thus EVERY map: handle<->VisNote, rest<->glyph, post-edit reselection, pitch-drag) for all LATER measures. Proved against real Verovio: a `quarter + forward(3)` bar gave model m2=0.5s vs Verovio 2.0s. FIX (one line, `src/edit-model.ts`): also fold `cursor` into `measureMaxCursor` after a `<forward>` (a `<backup>` reduces cursor so it never raises the max). Regression tests in `edit-model.test.ts`: trailing-`<forward>` bar AND a short-trailing-voice grand-staff bar both land m2 at 2.0s. The note-driven MAX (Case A2: voice 1 fills the bar, voice 2 ends short) was already correct and verified against real Verovio. 496 tests green (was 494). Remaining-onset caveat (NOT fixed, pathological): a `<divisions>` change MID-measure mixes units in `measureMaxCursor`; no real score does this and Verovio likely also breaks.

- **2026-06-04 - BUGFIX (feat/edit-add, uncommitted): clicking a REST was a no-op on the SHIPPED demo (and any MULTI-MEASURE score). TWO independent root causes, both masked because every prior edit fixture was a SINGLE measure.** Proved in node by driving the real toolkit + real model on `public/demo.musicxml` (a 4-measure C scale, trailing half rest): model rest `onsetSec=2, staff=1` vs Verovio `timeSec=8, staff=4`, so `buildRestIndexToId` returned an EMPTY map and `idToRestIndex.get(restG.id)` was `undefined` (the defensive bail in `main.ts` rest pointerdown).
  - **Cause 1 (model onset was MEASURE-RELATIVE, not absolute).** `reindexHandles` reset `cursor=0` each measure, so every measure's first event sat back at onset 0; the doc comment CLAIMED absolute but the code did not. VisNote[] (score.ts) and the Verovio timemap are ABSOLUTE from the score start, so handle/rest onsets only matched in a 1-measure score. FIX: accumulate `measureStartQuarters` per part (in QUARTERS, divisions-independent so a mid-piece `<divisions>` change stays right) and add it; advance it at each measure end by the measure's MAX forward cursor (handles `<backup>`/`<forward>` voice interleave). `beat` stays measure-relative. `src/edit-model.ts`. This ALSO repaired latent multi-measure breakage in `buildHandleToVisIndex` (delete + pitch re-derive in bars 2+), the post-add / post-undo re-selection, and the pitch-drag preview highlight (all key on `onsetSec` vs an absolute VisNote/Verovio time).
  - **Cause 2 (Verovio staff ordinal was DOCUMENT-WIDE, not within-measure).** Verovio lays a score out as `g.system > (g.measure > g.staff > g.layer)*`, so a `g.staff` group repeats ONCE PER MEASURE. `restStavesFromSvg` counted staff groups document-wide, so a rest in measure 4 of a single-staff score read "staff 4". The `g.staff` tag carries NO `@n`/`data-n`, and MEI `<staff n>` xml:ids do not always equal the SVG `<g>` ids, so the number must come from the SVG STRUCTURE. FIX: reset the staff count at each `g.measure` open; a staff's musical number is its ordinal WITHIN its measure (verified: a 2-staff 2-measure score still resolves a measure-2 staff-2 rest to staff 2, not 4). `src/verovio-view.ts`.
  - **REGRESSION COVERAGE:** `edit-model-integration.test.ts` now loads the REAL `public/demo.musicxml`, asserts its rest maps to a glyph (onset absolute > 6s, staff 1) and round-trips through fill (addNote engraves a note + no rest; removeNote restores + re-maps), plus a 2-staff multi-measure case proving staff-2 disambiguation. Pure guards: `edit-model.test.ts` pins absolute onsets across 2 bars; `verovio-view.test.ts` pins `restStavesFromSvg` within-measure counting (single-staff 4-measure stays staff 1; grand staff still gives staff 2). 494 tests green (was 488; +6), typecheck + build green. Earlier ADD-a-note entry below is now superseded on the staff-ordinal detail.

- **2026-06-04 - SMART EDIT: ADD-A-NOTE v1 shipped (fill a rest -> note of the same duration, the inverse of delete) + two P2 review fixes. Branch `feat/edit-add`. NOT committed (left in the worktree for in-browser verification). 488 JS tests green (was 442; +46), typecheck + build green.** Pitch editing, delete, undo/redo, dual-surface sync, and edit-mode-OFF-as-a-true-no-op are all untouched. Design spec: `design.md` "ADD-A-NOTE v1" (ratified). To VERIFY in a browser: enter edit mode on a score with a rest, click the rest glyph on the STAFF (it shows a brass halo + an "Add a note" button; rests do NOT appear on the falling canvas), press the button or Enter/N to convert it to a note, then Up/Down (or drag, or +/-) to adjust the new note's pitch, Ctrl+Z to undo (the rest returns). Keyboard-only path: Left/Right now walks rests too (interleaved by onset), Enter fills, Up/Down pitches.
  - **MODEL = a SEPARATE rest registry, NOT a NoteHandle (the load-bearing decision).** `reindexHandles()` already walked rests (computing onset/duration) but pushed no handle; it now ALSO builds a parallel `restHandles[]` (id = document position among rests, + `el`/`onsetSec`/`durationSec`/`durationDivs`/`type`/`staff`/`voice`/`beat`) and `restFifths[]`. Because a rest is NOT a `NoteHandle`, everything iterating pitched notes (the staff/canvas note maps, the pitched-note count, delete/pitch/undo keying) is byte-for-byte unchanged; the rest is only selectable + convertible. `ScoreModel` gained `restHandles`, `addNote(restId, pitch): AddRecord|null`, `removeNote(record)`, `fifthsForRest(id)`, and `restDurationName(type)` (for the announce). `src/edit-model.ts`.
  - **`makeNoteFrom(restEl, pitch, fifths)` is the literal mirror of `makeRestFrom`** (rest -> note): builds a `<note>` with `<pitch>` (+ a key-sig-synced `<accidental>`, same rule as `setPitch`: print one only when the pitch departs from the key's default for its letter), preserving the rest's `<duration>`/`<voice>`/`<type>`/dots/`<staff>` IN PLACE (fixed-bar, no timing math), dropping the `<rest/>`. `addNote` = clone the rest (for undo) + `makeNoteFrom` + replaceChild + reindex; `removeNote` = swap the rest clone back in (literally the standalone-delete restore path). `AddNoteCommand` mirrors `DeleteNoteCommand` (apply RE-DERIVES the `AddRecord` on every call incl. redo since the conversion is deterministic; carries a `VisNoteSnapshot` only main.ts reads). `src/edit-commands.ts`.
  - **REST GLYPH <-> model rest mapping = (onset seconds, staff), via the timemap + the SVG staff nesting** (the genuinely new render plumbing). PROVED against the real toolkit (throwaway probes, deleted): Verovio emits rests as `<g class="rest" id="...">`; `getTimeForElement(restId)` is UNRELIABLE for rests (returns 0), so onsets come from a SEPARATE `renderToTimemap({includeRests:true})`'s `restsOn` arrays (`restOnsetsFromTimemap`), and the staff number from the rest `<g>`'s enclosing `<g class="staff">` ORDINAL in the SVG (staff 1 group first; `restStavesFromSvg`). `buildRestIndexToId(renderRests, modelRestHandles)` keys both sides on `restKey(onset, staff)` (first-wins on a 2-voice collision, like the note map). The CURSOR/stepTimes timemap stays `includeRests:false` (a rest is not a cursor stop) so the sync invariant is untouched; the rest-inclusive timemap feeds ONLY the rest map. `VerovioRender` gained `rests: VerovioRest[]`. `src/verovio-view.ts`.
  - **PITCH DEFAULTS (ADD-2, fewest steps).** MOUSE: the clicked staff line/space (the rest glyph's vertical CENTER = the staff middle line, B4 treble / D3 bass; each ~half-glyph-height of click offset = one diatonic step, key-sig aware). The rest pointerdown STASHES the click y (`lastRestPointer`, cleared on any other selection); the "Add a note" button uses it when it matches the selected rest, else the keyboard default. KEYBOARD (Enter/N): the PREVIOUS sounding note's pitch in the same voice/staff (nearest earlier onset), else the middle line. The pure choice logic is `src/edit-nav.ts` (`keyboardDefaultPitch`/`mouseDefaultPitch`); main.ts adapts handles into it. The new note becomes the shared selection immediately (found by (midi, onset) post-reindex) so the next arrow/drag/+/- nudges it via the existing P1 path.
  - **NO note-input mode (ADD-3, ratified).** The edit cluster CONTENTS swap on what is selected: a NOTE shows pitch-down/up + delete (unchanged); a REST shows ONE `#add-note-btn` "Add a note" + a readout naming the rest. **Enter** converts; **N** is a one-shot ALIAS (handled BEFORE the `selectedHandle===null` keydown guard since a rest selection has `selectedHandle===null`). A rest is a STAFF-ONLY target (rests do not fall): `sheetContainer` pointerdown resolves `g.note` first, then `g.rest` (direct hit OR nearest within a 12px-padded box = a >=24px finger target, since rest glyphs are tiny), gated by the same primary-button `e.isPrimary` check (a rest has no drag, so `shouldStartPitchDrag` is not consulted). Left/Right interleaves rests by onset (`staffNavOrder`/`stepStaffNav`, pure); canvas Up/Down stays notes-only. `selectedRest` is a SEPARATE selection slot (at most one of `selectedHandle`/`selectedRest` is set); Play/record clear BOTH.
  - **VISUAL (ADD-5).** A selected rest wears the SAME `.ph-selected` brass language (the CSS now targets `g.rest.ph-selected` identically to `g.note.ph-selected`, sized to the rest bbox); an unselected rest gets `cursor:pointer` + a faint ~20% accent wash on hover/focus. The add is discrete (no drag preview): the halo moves from the rest to the new notehead and the falling bar appears in the same re-engrave. Staff `aria-label` gained the rest clause; announcements (shared `#edit-live`): select "Selected a quarter rest, beat 3"; add "Added a note, D5"; undo "Removed the note"; redo "Added a note, D5".
  - **HAND of the fill** = copy an existing note's hand on the rest's staff (the authority; matches score.ts incl. the single-staff "unknown" case), else the staff convention only for a genuine grand staff (`handForRestStaff`). Avoids a subtle velocity/mute mislabel from naively mapping staff 1 -> right on a single-staff score.
  - **P2 REVIEW FIX 1 - redo-of-delete selection parity.** `redoDelete` picked the next selection by DOCUMENT position (`handles[handleId] ?? handles[handleId-1]`) while `deleteSelectedNote` picks by MUSICAL order (onset then midi), so on a grand staff (document order != musical order) they diverged. Now `redoDelete` uses `musicalNeighborAfterDelete` (pure, `src/edit-nav.ts`: "next note in (onset,midi), else previous") evaluated over the post-delete handles from the deleted note's (onset, midi), so delete and redo select IDENTICALLY. Tested incl. the grand-staff divergence case.
  - **P2 REVIEW FIX 2 - `FIRST_MIDI` constant.** The clamp announce in main.ts used a hardcoded `21`; now imports + uses `FIRST_MIDI` (re-exported from `edit-model.ts`, which already imported it from `piano.ts`).
  - **TESTS:** `edit-model.test.ts` (rest registry parse, `makeNoteFrom`/`addNote`/`removeNote` round-trip + fixed-bar + accidental sync in C and D major, the added note maps by (midi,onset), `restDurationName`); `edit-commands.test.ts` (`AddNoteCommand` apply/invert/redo + LIFO with delete; stub model gained `restHandles`/`addNote`/`removeNote`/`fifthsForRest`); `verovio-view.test.ts` (`parseSvgRestIds`, `restOnsetsFromTimemap`, `restStavesFromSvg`, `restKey`, `buildRestIndexToId` incl. staff disambiguation + collision); `edit-nav.test.ts` (NEW: nav interleave/step, both pitch defaults key-sig aware, the musical-neighbor P2 fix); `edit-model-integration.test.ts` (rest maps to a real glyph + `addNote`/`removeNote` through real Verovio).
  - **GOTCHA - render-path has NO CI; ALWAYS verify with the real toolkit.** The rest id/onset/staff extraction (timemap shape, SVG `<g class="staff">` nesting) is engine-specific and untested by typecheck; it is proved by the integration test + was probed against the installed Verovio 6.2.0. If Verovio changes the `restsOn` timemap key or the staff-group nesting, rest selection silently degrades to "no halo / unmapped rest" (never crashes: `buildRestIndexToId` just leaves it unmapped). FOLLOW-UP: P3 duration (arbitrary-duration insertion, splitting a rest, entering on an empty beat with no rest) is still the next increment; v1 can only fill an EXISTING rest (the honest, scanner-matched limit).

  - **DELETE = a FIXED-BAR DOM edit on the model, NOT a VisNote removal.** New `ScoreModel.deleteNote(id): DeleteRecord | null` + `restoreNote(record)` in `src/edit-model.ts`. Three branches, all preserving the measure's time extent (proven by `measureFilledDivs` in the test, which walks the cursor with `<backup>`/`<forward>` so the grand staff's two parallel voices read extent 8, not 16): (1) a STANDALONE note becomes a `<rest>` of the same `<duration>`/`<type>`/`<voice>`/`<dot>`*/`<staff>` IN PLACE (`makeRestFrom`); (2) a `<chord/>` MEMBER is REMOVED (a rest cannot stack in a chord; the chord's onset note still advances the cursor, so the bar is unchanged); (3) a chord ONSET note with following members is REMOVED after PROMOTING the next member to onset (stripping its `<chord/>`) so the duration-advance survives. Every branch drops exactly one pitched handle, so the VisNote count falls by one. The rest is not a VisNote, so it leaves the falling notes + audio.
  - **HANDLE IDS ARE NO LONGER INDEX-STABLE UNDER DELETE - the model RE-INDEXES.** The P1 invariant "a handle id is a permanent session id" held only because pitch edits never add/remove notes. Delete breaks it, so the parse-walk was extracted into a `reindexHandles()` closure that clears + refills the SAME live `handles[]` array (which `model.handles` aliases) after every structural edit. A handle id is therefore "the note at this document position"; restoring re-inserts the cloned `<note>` at its original DOM position, so the restored note reclaims its original id. The delete command keys on that position for undo/redo.
  - **INVERSION = a DOM CLONE captured at delete time.** `DeleteRecord` holds a deep clone of the original `<note>`, its parent + nextSibling (for re-insertion), the rest placeholder (replace-in-place case), and the promoted member + its stripped `<chord/>` (promotion case). `restoreNote` reverses the promotion first, then swaps the clone back in (for the rest) or re-inserts it at its position (for a removal), then re-indexes. `applyCommand`/`invertCommand` (`src/edit-commands.ts`) gained a `DeleteNoteCommand`; apply RE-DERIVES the record on every call (initial push AND redo) since deletion is deterministic, so redo reproduces the removal. The command also carries a `VisNoteSnapshot` (a DOM-free duck type, so the command stack stays model-agnostic + unit-testable) that ONLY main.ts reads, to splice the deleted falling note out on delete and back in at its index on undo.
  - **main.ts wiring:** `deleteSelectedNote()` captures the deleted VisNote + picks the neighbor to select BY DOM ELEMENT (immune to the reindex) before pushing the command, splices `score.notes`, re-finds the neighbor's new handle id post-delete, and routes through `finishEdit(announce, explicitNotes)` (new optional arg: a structural edit supplies the already-spliced array verbatim instead of the same-length pitch projection). `doUndo`/`doRedo` branch on `cmd.kind`: undo of a delete splices the VisNote back at its slot + re-selects the restored handle (`Restored D5`); redo re-deletes + selects the note now at the deleted position. Re-added the `#delete-note-btn` trash button (`index.html`) + click wiring + the Delete/Backspace keydown branch (needs a selection); BOTH surface aria-labels say "Delete removes it" again.
  - **FIX 1 - 88-KEY CLAMP (MIDI 21..108).** `diatonicStep`/`chromaticStep`/`octaveStep` now return the UNCHANGED pitch when the candidate would fall off the keyboard (new `pitchInRange` + `FIRST_MIDI`/`LAST_MIDI` from `piano.ts`). The drag paths are clamped by construction (staff drag repeats `diatonicStep`; canvas drag snaps to `keyAtX` which only yields real keys). `commitPitchEdit` detects the no-op (same MIDI) and announces "Already at the lowest/highest key." without pushing a command.
  - **FIX 2 - DRAG-START GATED on the primary LEFT button.** New pure `src/edit-pointer.ts` `shouldStartPitchDrag(e)` = `button === 0 && isPrimary && pointerType !== "touch"` (split out so it is unit-testable without booting main.ts). Both surface `pointerdown` handlers ignore non-primary pointers entirely, SELECT on a primary press, but only `beginStaffDrag`/`beginCanvasDrag` when the gate passes - so a right-click or a touch-scroll that starts on a note selects (or does nothing) but never hijacks into a drag. A plain primary left click still selects + arms a drag.
  - **TESTS:** delete + undo/redo round-trip, fixed-bar extent preserved, chord-member removal, chord-onset promotion, map rebuild, out-of-range no-op (`edit-model.test.ts`); the clamp on all three step axes (`edit-model.test.ts`); the delete command apply/invert/redo + LIFO with a pitch edit (`edit-commands.test.ts`, stub model gained `deleteNote`/`restoreNote`); the delete render-drop + restore through REAL Verovio (`edit-model-integration.test.ts`); the drag gate (`edit-pointer.test.ts`).
  - **FOLLOW-UPS:** P2's other half = ADD-a-note (model-level). P3 = duration (the hard one; needs a full re-extract since times change). The `note-edit.ts` `recomputeDuration` STAYS (used by `reloadNotes`); the old VisNote-only `deleteNote` stayed pulled (this delete is model-level).

- **2026-06-04 - DELETE PULLED FROM SMART EDIT P1 (the stopgap was a sync-invariant violation).** The P1 delete stopgap (Designer P1-4) called the VisNote-only `deleteNote`: it removed the note from the falling view but the staff (driven by the model) still showed it, and it was outside the command stack so it was not undoable. That desyncs the two surfaces and breaks single-source-of-truth, so delete is REMOVED from P1 entirely; proper model-level delete (syncs both surfaces, undoable, fixed-bar rest-filling) is a P2 increment. Removed: the `#delete-note-btn` from the edit toolbar in `index.html`, the button decl + click wiring + the Delete/Backspace keydown branch + `deleteSelectedNote()` in `src/main.ts`, and `deleteNote` + its 2 tests from `note-edit.ts`/`note-edit.test.ts` (now unused; `recomputeDuration` STAYS, still used by `reloadNotes` after a pitch edit). BOTH surface application aria-labels dropped the "Delete removes it" clause. Pitch editing, undo/redo, dual-surface drag, and the Correct-mode removal are untouched. Left in the worktree, not committed. 421 JS tests green (was 423; -2 delete tests), typecheck + build green. NOTE: the forward-looking Delete rows in `docs/context/design.md` (Designer) and the `#delete-note-btn` QA-handle list in `docs/context/qa.md` still mention delete; those are other roles' files (design.md's are the P2 spec) and were left for the Designer/QA to reconcile.

- **2026-06-04 - SMART EDIT MODE P1 BUILT: DUAL-SURFACE pitch editing on one source-of-truth model, undo/redo, Correct mode retired. Branch `feat/edit-pitch`. NOT committed (left in the worktree for in-browser verification). 423 JS tests green (was 389; +34), typecheck + build green.** New code: `src/edit-model.ts` (the editable notation model), `src/edit-commands.ts` (invertible command stack), `buildVisIndexToId` + `visIndexToId` added to `src/verovio-view.ts`, `keyAtX` in `src/piano.ts`, drag-preview/mirror-deemphasis/`midiAtX` on `src/visualizer.ts`, the whole dual-surface rewrite in `src/main.ts`, docked edit-toolbar + undo/redo/delete buttons in `index.html`, styles in `src/style.css`. New tests: `edit-model.test.ts` (27), `edit-commands.test.ts` (8), `edit-model-integration.test.ts` (3, real WASM), plus `keyAtX` + `buildVisIndexToId` cases.
  - **MODEL APPROACH = pitch-targeted mutation over the retained `sourceMusicXml` DOM (NOT a from-scratch model).** `parseScoreModel(xml, bpmOverride?)` parses the MusicXML into a DOM and indexes every pitched `<note>` element in document order as a stable HANDLE, computing each handle's onset-seconds + MIDI + spelling by walking the part the way score.ts does (divisions, `<backup>`/`<forward>`, chords share an onset, tie continuations flagged). `setPitch(id, {step,octave,alter})` rewrites the `<note>`'s `<pitch>` children (and syncs the `<accidental>` glyph to the key sig) IN PLACE; `serialize()` re-emits MusicXML for Verovio. Chosen over a custom model because P1 pitch is a clean LOCAL edit with no reflow, so DOM surgery round-trips cleanly and is the smallest correct change; it is EXTENSIBLE to P3 duration (mutate `<duration>`/`<type>` + a bar-sum validator over the same measure structure). The spike's warning against XML surgery was specifically about duration/rest/tie, not pitch. Verovio has NO MusicXML export, so the model (our DOM), not Verovio's MEI, is the source of truth (matches the ratified architecture).
  - **THE SPINE = a stable HANDLE id mapped to the VisNote index by (midi, onset).** Pitch-only editing never adds/removes/reorders `<note>` elements, so a handle's index in the pitched-note list is a permanent session id the command stack keys on. handle <-> VisNote index is rebuilt after every edit via `buildHandleToVisIndex` (the SAME (midi, onset-seconds) keying `verovio-view.ts` uses), and VisNote index -> staff notehead id uses the new `verovioRender.visIndexToId`. So handle <-> VisNote <-> Verovio-id are all pinned by (midi, onset); after a pitch edit the onset is unchanged so selection follows the note to its new pitch. Selection is stored as `selectedHandle` (durable across re-renders, unlike a VisNote index which a delete would shift).
  - **THE ROUND-TRIP (per edit): command -> model.setPitch -> re-engrave staff from `model.serialize()` (Verovio) + project the model's new pitch onto the falling VisNote[] (midi+spelling only; TIME/stepTimes are invariant under a pitch edit, so the sync invariant holds trivially) -> `reloadNotes` rebuilds audio+canvas (transport-safe) -> rebuild maps -> re-apply shared selection.** Verified end-to-end with the REAL WASM in `edit-model-integration.test.ts` (a model pitch edit re-renders the staff at the new pitch + accidentals engrave + handle re-maps). NOTE: P1 does NOT re-run OSMD/extractScore on an edit (pitch keeps every time, so stepTimes never change); it projects the changed midi/spelling onto the existing VisNote[]. P3 (duration) WILL need a full re-extract since times change.
  - **GOTCHA - map-ordering on UNDO (cost me a bug; guarded + tested).** `finishEdit` must project the model's pitch onto `score.notes` using the EXISTING (pre-edit) handle map (index-stable), THEN `reloadNotes` + rebuild the map against the updated notes. Rebuilding the map FIRST fails: after `commandStack.undo()` the model already holds the OLD pitch while `score.notes` still holds the NEW one, so `buildHandleToVisIndex` (by midi) would not match the just-reverted note and the undo would not reach the falling notes. So `doUndo`/`doRedo` do NOT call `rederiveMaps` before `finishEdit`. Pinned by `edit-model.test.ts` "re-derivation across edits + undo".
  - **GOTCHA - tempo agreement for the (midi, onset-SECONDS) key.** VisNote times use OSMD's `DefaultStartTempoInBpm || 120`; the model must scale onsets with the SAME bpm or the seconds will not match. `enterEditMode` passes `osmd.Sheet.DefaultStartTempoInBpm` into `parseScoreModel`. Verovio's timemap defaults to 120 for a no-tempo score (the common OMR case) and reads the same `<sound tempo>` otherwise, so the three agree in practice; if a score makes OSMD and Verovio disagree on tempo, later-onset notes may fail to map (degrades to staff-halo-only / no halo, never crashes). 1ms rounding tolerance on the key.
  - **DESIGN-vs-REALITY axis deviation (deliberate, documented in code).** The Designer spec describes the CANVAS pitch drag as VERTICAL (it imagined a horizontal piano-roll where pitch is vertical). This app's falling-notes canvas is VERTICAL: pitch is the HORIZONTAL axis (key columns), time is vertical. So the canvas pitch drag is HORIZONTAL (snap to the key column under the pointer via `visualizer.midiAtX`), vertical ignored. This preserves the spec's INTENT (drag the bar to a new pitch, snap to keys, time fixed) on the real geometry. Staff drag is vertical (correct: pitch is vertical on a staff), snapping in diatonic steps with a per-step px sensitivity derived from the notehead bbox (~half an interline), re-engraving the staff at each snapped step (single-digit ms). Surface asymmetry is intended: STAFF = diatonic (key-sig aware), CANVAS = chromatic (semitone).
  - **DRAG = one coalesced command.** During a drag only the active surface previews; the mirror holds the pre-edit state de-emphasized (~55%: canvas via `visualizer.setMirrorDeemphasis`, staff via a `.ph-mirror` class). The staff drag mutates the model directly for the live re-engrave preview, then rolls back to `beforePitch` on release and pushes ONE `setPitch` command (before->final) so apply is the single source of the change; the canvas drag only previews (model untouched) and computes the final pitch from the snapped key on release. Window-level `pointermove`/`pointerup` (not element-level) so a drag that leaves the surface, or a staff re-render that destroys the captured `<g>`, still tracks. Keyboard pitch edits are discrete (no preview): both surfaces + audio update at once.
  - **CORRECT MODE RETIRED + divergence machinery removed.** Deleted `#correct-btn`, `correctMode`, the canvas `edited` flag + dashed "edited" outline + the "Edited..." status line, `nudgePitch`/`hasEdits` (gone from `note-edit.ts`), and `#staff-edit-live` (collapsed into the ONE shared `#edit-live` region to avoid double-announce). `note-edit.ts` keeps ONLY `deleteNote` + `recomputeDuration` as the P1 delete STOPGAP. **DELETE is a known stopgap wart (ratified, Designer P1-4): it removes the VisNote only, NOT the model, so the staff still shows the deleted note and delete is NOT undoable in P1.** P2 upgrades delete to a model-level fixed-bar rest. Call this out to the user/PM.
  - **EDIT-MODE-OFF stays a TRUE no-op:** every new listener (pointerdown on canvas/sheet, the edit keydown, window pointermove/up) early-returns when `!editMode`/`!drag`; the model + command stack are null outside edit mode. The only non-editing-user change is an enabled-but-unclicked Edit button + a retained XML string. The docked `#edit-toolbar` lives inside `#sheet` but is `hidden` and exempt from the `.editing` hide rule; `#sheet:empty` was already defeated by the always-present `#sheet-labels` div, so the placeholder is unaffected.
  - **TIE-CONTINUATION click is a no-op (minor).** A tie continuation notehead maps to no VisNote (score.ts merges ties), so clicking it selects nothing rather than the tie start. Keyboard staff nav already excludes continuations. P2 polish.
  - **FOLLOW-UPS for later increments:** P2 = add-a-note + model-level delete (rest, undoable). P3 = duration (the hard one; needs full re-extract on edit since times change). Consider DOMPurify on the `verovioHost.innerHTML` sink once edits flow through (the P0 review flagged this as defense-in-depth; still not strictly needed since Verovio escapes output and we only feed it our own serialized model).

- **2026-06-04 - CODE REVIEW (pre-merge gate) of Smart Edit Mode P0 (`verovio-view.ts` + edit-mode wiring): SHIP, no blocking findings.** Verified the `loadScoreXml` rebase merge is correct: `sourceMusicXml = xml` set before `osmd.load`, button enablement is `hasSheet && sourceMusicXml !== null` and `loadNotes` sets `hasSheet` then calls `setEditButtonEnabled()`, so the order is right; the `{upgrade:true}` progressive path returns early via `upgradeNotes` (which does NOT call `setEditButtonEnabled`, but the button was already enabled and `sourceMusicXml` stays non-null, so it stays correctly enabled). Edit mode OFF is a true no-op (frame()/click/keydown/resize all gate on `editMode`; only changes for non-editing users are an enabled-but-unclicked button + a retained XML string in memory). Two SECURITY facts worth keeping:
  - **The `verovioHost.innerHTML = svg` sink is NOT an XSS risk in P0.** PROVED against the real toolkit (throwaway probes, now deleted): adversarial MusicXML (script/img/onerror payloads injected into work-title, credit-words, part-name, direction words, lyric text, and an `xml:id`) produces ZERO active content in the SVG. Verovio (a) escapes all emitted text (`A<B` -> `&lt;`, raw `<` never survives), (b) renders no titles/credits at all under the app's `header:"none"` option, (c) drops a malicious `xml:id` (must be a valid NCName), and (d) emits no `<script>`, no `on*=` handlers, no `<foreignObject>`, no `javascript:`/`<a>`/SMIL vectors (only internal `xlink:href="#glyph"`). Also, a `<script>` set via `div.innerHTML` does not execute per the HTML spec anyway; the real innerHTML-SVG hazards (event-handler attrs, foreignObject-with-HTML) are exactly what Verovio does not emit. NON-BLOCKING defense-in-depth for later: if the app ever renders user titles or flips header modes, or once P1 serializes an edited model back through Verovio, add a sanitize pass (DOMPurify w/ SVG profile) before the innerHTML sink.
  - **`npm audit`'s 1 critical + 4 moderate are dev-tooling, NOT verovio.** They are all in the vitest/vite/esbuild/vite-node/@vitest-mocker chain (critical = "Vitest UI server arbitrary file read+exec"; moderates = esbuild dev-server SSRF + vite path-traversal), they PRE-EXISTED on origin/main, and verovio itself has zero advisories. None are runtime-reachable in the shipped browser bundle (Vitest UI is never run; dev-server flaws don't ship). Confirmed the lazy `import("verovio/...")` code-splits: `npm run build` emits `verovio-module-*.js` (~7.9MB) + `verovio-*.js` (~7.6KB) as chunks SEPARATE from `main-*.js`, so non-editing users never download the WASM. 389 JS tests green (incl. 6 real-WASM integration + 16 pure), typecheck + build green. MINOR non-blocking: `renderVerovio` calls `updateVerovioPlayhead(...,true)` before `editMode=true` is set in `enterEditMode`, so the forced first-entry tint is a no-op (the rAF loop applies it ~16ms later); the `force` flag still works on the resize path where `editMode` is already true. Also the forced `exitEditMode()` on every `loadScoreXml` (incl. progressive upgrades) means a user who enters edit mode after the first partial gets kicked out on each later partial/complete - annoying but harmless in P0 (no edits to lose; progressive is default OFF). Both are P1 polish, not gates.

- **2026-06-04 - ADMIN feature-flag page: live OMR flag control via an R2-polled config, no restart.**
  `/admin` (a SECOND Vite HTML entry; `vite.config.ts` now declares `index.html` + `admin.html`, which
  Cloudflare Pages serves at `/` and `/admin`) lets the user toggle the 7 free OMR engine/delivery
  flags. Mechanism: the page POSTs the desired flags to `functions/api/flags.ts`, which writes
  `config/omr-flags.json` to R2; the always-on worker reads that object at the top of each poll cycle
  (`omr-worker/flag_config.py apply_overrides`) and applies the known flags onto `os.environ`. EVERY
  flag check in the worker stack already reads `os.environ` per job (`worker.*_enabled`,
  `reconcile.referee_enabled`, `llm_omr.llm_enabled`), so mutating `os.environ` is picked up uniformly
  with NO per-module change and NO restart. Original env captured once (`_ENV_DEFAULTS`) so a
  dropped/absent config reverts cleanly to the box env. ARCHITECTURE: the flag-KEY allowlist +
  validation + auth are ONE pure module `src/flags-server.ts` (`KNOWN_FLAGS`, `sanitizeFlagConfig`
  drops unknown keys + coerces "0"/"1", `isAuthorized` constant-time Bearer compare, fail-closed on an
  unset token); the UI METADATA (accuracy/latency/algorithm per flag, primitive->advanced tiers,
  dependency cascade `withFlag`) is `src/admin-flags.ts`; the page is `src/admin.ts` + `src/admin.css`
  (DOM glue, not unit-tested). `OMR_LLM` is EXCLUDED from the allowlist (paid), so it can never be
  enabled from the web. The TS `KNOWN_FLAGS` and the Python `flag_config.KNOWN_FLAGS` are locked
  together by a JS source-guard test (`flags-server.test.ts` reads the .py as text). Browser-verified
  end-to-end (token gate -> cards seeded from a mocked GET -> toggle + dependency cascade -> Save POSTs
  the full 7-flag config), 0 console errors. Tests: `flags-server.test.ts`, `admin-flags.test.ts`,
  `test_flag_config.py`. MANUAL step: set the `ADMIN_TOKEN` Secret in the Cloudflare Pages dashboard
  (infrastructure.md). DEFAULT-neutral: the page does nothing to prod until the token is set + a flag
  toggled.

- **2026-06-04 - PROGRESSIVE OMR (partial-result protocol + fast-then-refine + per-page streaming).**
  The worker writes the result key MULTIPLE times per job so the browser renders the first notes while
  the rest computes. In-progress writes carry `omr-status="partial"` + `omr-version` INSIDE the
  MusicXML (`omr-worker/progressive.py` `stamp_partial`); the final write is unmarked (= complete).
  Mirrors the failure-sentinel pattern, so `functions/api/omr/result.ts` is UNCHANGED (200 for partial
  and complete alike; the marker rides in the body + R2 object metadata). Pure never-raise helpers in
  `progressive.py` (`stamp_partial` + `append_measures`); orchestration in `process_job` behind two
  flags: `OMR_PROGRESSIVE` (fast-then-refine: publish geom's pitch-only partial the moment its future
  resolves while Clarity still runs CONCURRENTLY, then the fused complete - no total-latency
  regression) and `OMR_PROGRESSIVE_PAGES` (per-page: `split_pdf_pages` via `pdfseparate`, then
  transcribe + fuse each page INDEPENDENTLY so there is no cross-engine measure alignment to get wrong,
  `append_measures` + publish per page). Idempotency moved to R2 object metadata: `result_is_complete`
  (renamed from `result_exists`) skips a job only when a COMPLETE result exists, so a crash
  mid-progressive reprocesses instead of stranding at a partial; the upload is deleted ONLY after the
  complete write. CLIENT (`src/omr.ts`): `pollOmrResult` gained `onPartial` (version-deduped, awaited);
  it still RESOLVES only on the complete result, so a caller without `onPartial` is unchanged.
  `main.ts`: `scanSheet` drops the blocking overlay + re-enables controls on the FIRST partial, shows a
  "Refining the rest..." status, and UPGRADES IN PLACE on later partials + the complete via the new
  `upgradeNotes` (preserves play state, the ABSOLUTE playhead clamped to the new duration, mutes /
  balance / tempo / name; re-renders the sheet). Extracted `createPart` to share the Tone.Part build
  across `loadNotes` / `reloadNotes` / `upgradeNotes`. A superseded job aborts (the poll's
  `isCancelledRequested` also checks `generation !== jobGeneration`) since controls re-enable mid-job.
  Browser-verified end-to-end with a mocked backend (partial -> "Refining..." -> complete upgrade, 0
  console errors). Tests: `test_progressive.py` (11), progressive worker tests in `test_worker.py`
  (17), `omr.test.ts` onPartial (6). Source-guard `omr-worker.test.ts` updated for the new final-write
  call site (`_put_result(..., complete=True)`). DEFAULT OFF; rollout/rollback in infrastructure.md.

- **2026-06-04 - SMART EDIT MODE P0 SHIPPED (read-only Verovio viewer + notehead selection behind an Edit flag; NO editing). `verovio@6.2.0` is now a SAVED dep. New code: `src/verovio-view.ts` (lazy-load + render + PURE sync/mapping helpers), `src/types/verovio.d.ts` (the package ships no types and `@types/verovio` is not installed, so a scoped ambient decl covers only the methods P0 uses), edit-mode wiring in `src/main.ts`, styles in `src/style.css`, an Edit button + Verovio credit in `index.html`. Tests: `src/verovio-view.test.ts` (16 pure-logic) + `src/verovio-integration.test.ts` (6, drives the REAL WASM in vitest's node env). 360 JS tests green, typecheck + build green.**
  - **IN-BROWSER under Vite is SOUND (the spike's open question).** The lazy `import("verovio/wasm")` + `import("verovio/esm")` code-splits cleanly: `npm run build` emits `verovio-module-*.js` (~7.9MB) + `verovio-*.js` (~7.6KB) as SEPARATE chunks from the main bundle, so non-editing users never download the payload. KEY FACT: the WASM is EMBEDDED in `verovio-module.mjs` as a decoded binary string literal (`findWasmBinary(){return binaryDecode('...')}`, `getBinarySync(file){return file}`); there is NO external `.wasm` file, so there is NOTHING for Vite to mis-resolve or 404 on. The build prints a benign warning: `Module "node:module" has been externalized for browser compatibility` - that `await import("node:module")` (createRequire) is gated behind `if (ENVIRONMENT_IS_NODE)` (false in a browser), so the externalized empty stub is never touched at runtime. No vite.config change was needed.
  - **API SHAPE CORRECTIONS vs the spike's recall (verified against the installed package via a throwaway node script run from INSIDE the repo - a bare `verovio` import does NOT resolve from a script OUTSIDE the repo, the spike's gotcha (b)).** (1) `getMIDIValuesForElement(id)` returns the note's values at the TOP LEVEL `{ pitch, duration, time }` (pitch = MIDI number), NOT `{ pitches: [...] }`. `src/verovio-view.ts` reads `.pitch`. (2) `renderToTimemap({ includeMeasures: true })` adds a measure-BOUNDARY marker entry (e.g. tstamp 2000 at the end of a 4/4 bar) on top of the note onsets, so our `stepTimes[]` analogue includes that end-of-measure stop (harmless extra cursor stop; the integration test asserts `[0,0.5,1,1.5,2]` for a 1-bar fixture). (3) ESM init is `const VerovioModule = await (await import("verovio/wasm")).default(); new (await import("verovio/esm")).VerovioToolkit(VerovioModule)`. Confirmed: 120bpm default tempo (matches `score.ts`), so timemap ms / 1000 == VisNote seconds, which is why the id<->VisNote key (midi, onset-seconds rounded to 1ms) lines up.
  - **id -> VisNote MAPPING (the consistency contract): key on (midi, onset seconds), first-wins.** Chords disambiguate by pitch at a shared onset. The one known gap is TIES: `score.ts` MERGES tie continuations into the start note (one bar), so only the tie-START segment shares an onset with a VisNote; continuation ids find no match and are simply absent from the map (caller falls back to id-only "note" label). This is the intended "where possible" behavior, unit-tested.
  - **DOM GOTCHA: OSMD wraps its SVG in an inner `div#osmdCanvasPageN` (confirmed in the installed min.js), so a `#sheet.editing > svg` selector would MISS it.** Edit mode renders the Verovio SVG into a `#verovio-host` div appended to `#sheet`, adds `.editing` to `#sheet`, and hides siblings with `#sheet.editing > *:not(#verovio-host)`. OSMD owns `#sheet` and an `osmd.load`/`render` between edit sessions can DETACH our host, so `renderVerovio` re-appends it if `parentNode !== sheetContainer` (else the SVG would render into an orphan). The toolkit instance is cached across enter/exit for fast re-entry; only the on-screen render is torn down on exit.
  - **MODE INTERACTIONS:** Edit mode is a NEW button ALONGSIDE Correct (P0 must not retire the #6 falling-canvas editor; the design's "retire Correct" step is a later increment, gated on edit mode being solid). Entering Edit pauses playback and exits Correct (mutually exclusive). In edit mode Left/Right step the STAFF selection (not the transport, which is paused). Playback still works with a timemap-driven brass playhead tint on the staff; selection during playback is harmless since P0 has no editing. Audio scores have no MusicXML -> Edit button stays disabled (`editModeAvailable = hasSheet && sourceMusicXml !== null`). Source MusicXML is now RETAINED in `sourceMusicXml` (was discarded as a local in `loadScoreXml`); cleared on audio load.
  - **NEXT (P1): pitch editing on the staff.** Needs the in-house notation model + command-undo, then the edit -> serialize-to-MusicXML -> `loadData` -> re-render -> re-derive VisNote[]/stepTimes -> rebuild Tone.Part loop (reuse `reloadNotes`). The geom+Clarity fusion is prod-primary with weak rhythm, so DURATION editing (P3) is the highest-value increment but hardest; do pitch first to exercise the whole loop on the easy axis.

- **2026-06-04 - VEROVIO VALIDATION SPIKE on our ACTUAL OMR output shape (throwaway, worktree-only, NO commit, NO production code, `npm install verovio --no-save` so package.json untouched). VERDICT: GO. Verovio (6.2.0, LGPLv3) does everything the staff-editor needs: faithful round-trip of un-edited elements, a clean id-based sync map + hit-testing that replaces our OSMD glue, and render latency low enough that live drag can re-render per frame.** Probe lived in `C:/tmp/verovio-spike/` (`probe.mjs` + `probe2.mjs` + `omr-sample.musicxml`); driven via the ESM build `verovio/wasm` (`dist/verovio-module.mjs`) + `verovio/esm` (`dist/verovio.mjs`). The toolkit method surface matches the official docs exactly.
  - **FIXTURE NOTE (honest): no real OMR `.musicxml` is committed in the repo** (only `public/demo.musicxml`, a trivial clean C scale; no `.mscz`/`.mscx`; the tctab/icarus/reverie pieces exist only as eval inputs/truth on the cx33, not as committed XML), and running the real OMR pipeline here is not feasible (no oemer/Clarity/geom model, GPU-free box). So I hand-built a MESSY-OMR fixture that mirrors the EXACT shape `omr-worker/llm_omr.py:score_json_to_musicxml` emits in prod: one `<part>` with `<staves>2</staves>`, treble G/2 + bass F/4, per measure staff-1 events -> `<backup>` -> staff-2, `<chord/>` members, `<tie>`/`<tied>`. Plus, on purpose, every v1-NON-edited element we must preserve (beams, slurs, ties, dynamics via `<direction>`, tuplets, repeat barlines, fermata, staccato) AND real-OMR mess: a 3-flat key sig with accidentals, a mid-piece treble->bass clef change, and one bar (m3) that does NOT add up (staff-1 sums to 3 beats in 4/4). Fidelity on messy input is the actual question, so the fixture is deliberately adversarial; it is NOT a clean publisher file. Re-run against a captured real OMR output when one is available, but the shape is faithful.
  - **(1) ROUND-TRIP FIDELITY = PASS, and EXPORT IS MEI-ONLY (load-bearing for the pipeline).** `loadData(MusicXML)` -> `getMEI()` -> reload that MEI -> re-render: musical content is preserved EXACTLY. Proof beyond eyeballing: the timemap "timing skeleton" (every onset time in ms + how many notes start at each onset) is byte-identical between the MusicXML-load and the MEI-reload (25 onset events, 38 total note onsets, last event 10000ms in both); a SECOND round-trip is element-count-stable (no drift). All preserved-element classes survived as proper MEI containers: beams 2 (one MEI `<beam>` per beamed group), slur 1, tie 1, tuplet 1, dynam 2, fermata 1, artic 1, chord 2, notes 21, clefs 3 (incl. the mid-piece change), keySig 2. **Watch out for the COUNT-SHAPE difference, it is NOT loss:** MusicXML tags beam/slur/tie/tuplet on EVERY note (begin/continue/end, start/stop), MEI uses ONE span/container element, so 6 MXL `<beam>` tags -> 2 MEI `<beam>`, 2 MXL slur tags -> 1, 3 MXL tie tags -> 1, 2 MXL tuplet tags -> 1, 4 `<chord/>` members -> 2 `<chord>`. Repeats round-trip cleanly (`measure @left="rptstart"`, `@right="rptend"`, final `@right="end"`). The UNDER-FILLED bar is handled GRACEFULLY: Verovio neither padded with rests, dropped notes, nor rejected the document; m3 kept exactly its 4 notes as-is (load-bearing, since real OMR bars routinely do not add up). One correct-notation behavior to expect: a redundant accidental is dropped when the key sig already implies it (Eb in 3 flats prints no flat), pitch unchanged. **MEI-ONLY EXPORT (confirmed via probe enumeration AND the official toolkit-methods doc): there is NO MusicXML export anywhere (no getMusicXML/renderToMusicXML); out-formats are MEI, Humdrum, PAE, MIDI, SVG, Timemap only.** CONSEQUENCE for the architecture: do NOT treat Verovio as a MusicXML<->MusicXML transform. In the recommended design (our own notation model is the source of truth, we SERIALIZE to MusicXML and feed Verovio purely as render+sync), this is a non-issue: the edited result is OUR model, not Verovio's MEI. If any downstream step ever needs MusicXML BACK FROM Verovio's MEI, there is no built-in path (would need an MEI->MusicXML converter elsewhere). Re-deriving `VisNote[]`/`stepTimes[]` from the model does not need it.
  - **(2) SYNC MAP + HIT-TESTING = PASS, and CLEANER than today's OSMD SVG-walking.** After `renderToMIDI()`, `renderToTimemap({includeMeasures,includeRests})` returns per-onset entries `{tstamp(ms), qstamp, on:[ids], off:[ids], measureOn}`. The equivalent of `score.ts` `stepTimes[]` is the sorted-unique set of `tstamp` values (verified: a clean 27-step list 0,250,333,500,...,10000ms incl. the triplet's 333/667). `getElementsAtTime(ms)` returns `{notes:[ids], chords:[ids], rests:[ids], measure, page}` (the cursor lookup; chords are a DISTINCT array so click-select can target a chord vs a single note). `getTimeForElement(id)` is the inverse (note id -> onset ms). HIT-TESTING is the big upgrade: every notehead in the rendered SVG is a `<g class="note" id="...">` whose id is the SAME stable xml:id as in the MEI model, so click->model-note is a direct id lookup. Verified: 21 of 21 MEI note ids are present as SVG `<g>` ids, and `getElementsAtTime(0).notes` ids are present in the SVG DOM (time->element->DOM closes). This REPLACES `sheet-overlay.ts` `readNotePositions`/`getSVGGElement` (which depends on the undocumented VexFlow `GraphicalNote.getSVGGElement()` + bbox walking through OSMD's `GraphicSheet.MeasureList`): with Verovio you query the model id and `getElementById` in the SVG, no graphical-tree walk. The sync invariant survives the renderer swap by construction (cursor + falling notes both derive from the one timemap).
  - **(3) RENDER LATENCY = PASS, fast enough for per-frame drag (no ghost-render needed on this size).** Warm-cache wall-clock on the prod grand-staff shape (beamed RH eighths over a LH whole-note chord), Node 24 / WASM, this machine: 8 measures (1 page) loadData 17.8ms + renderAllPages 6.6ms = 24ms; 16 meas (1pg) 23.4+8.7=32ms; 24 meas (1pg) 27.5+11.8=39ms; **32 meas (2 PAGES) loadData 36.9ms + render both pages 16.7ms = 54ms**. Crucially, RE-RENDER-ONLY of an already-loaded page (the live-drag inner loop) is 1.8-4.5ms across those sizes, i.e. 200+ fps. So full reload+render of a 2-page score is ~50ms (fine for an on-drop re-render) and a re-render of the current page after an in-memory model tweak is single-digit ms (fine for per-frame drag). The S3 "ghost-and-re-render-on-drop" mitigation is NOT required for 1-2 page scores; revisit only for very large multi-page scores. Note browser WASM will differ from Node; re-measure in-app, but the headroom is large.
  - **LICENSE = OK under the free-tooling rule, with ONE practical requirement: LGPLv3 (`LGPL-3.0-or-later` in the package; confirmed at book.verovio.org/introduction/licensing). Free for commercial web use; the requirement is VISIBLE CREDIT to Verovio on the site (and, only if we modify the Verovio library itself, publish those changes). We do not modify the library (we drive it as-is), so the only obligation is an attribution line in the UI/about. No paid tier, no caps.**
  - **BLOCKERS / SURPRISES: none blocking.** Minor: (a) the npm install pulls a transient `prebuild-install` deprecation warning and `npm audit` flags moderate/critical advisories in install-time deps (the WASM bundle itself is prebuilt; revisit audit before adding it for real, but it is not a runtime-code concern). (b) ESM import of a probe script located OUTSIDE the repo cannot resolve the bare `verovio/wasm`/`verovio/esm` specifiers (Node resolves from the script's dir, not cwd); use absolute `file://` paths to `dist/verovio-module.mjs` + `dist/verovio.mjs`, or put the script in the repo. In-app (Vite, bundler-resolved) this is a non-issue. (c) WASM payload is multi-MB (`verovio-module.mjs` ~7MB) -> lazy-load on first entry to edit mode as already planned. NET: Verovio is validated as the render+sync engine for the staff editor; proceed with the staged plan (P0 viewer parity behind a flag, then pitch edit, etc.).

- **2026-06-04 - SMART EDIT MODE feasibility spike (edit the staff notation directly; sheet becomes single source of truth that the falling notes + audio re-derive from). RECOMMENDATION: build our own editable NOTATION model + render with VEROVIO; do NOT try to make OSMD an editor. Architecture spike only, no production code written.**
  - **Why this is a new kind of state, not an extension of `note-edit.ts`.** Today the flow is ONE-WAY: MusicXML -> `osmd.load` -> `extractScore` walks the cursor -> `VisNote[]` (flat performance model in seconds; no measures/note-values/voices). The source XML is DISCARDED (`xml` is a local in `loadScoreXml` at `src/main.ts:461`, gone after `osmd.load`). Existing edits (`nudgePitch`/`deleteNote` in `src/note-edit.ts`) mutate the `VisNote[]` ONLY and deliberately DIVERGE from the sheet (sheet stays authoritative; falling notes get a dashed "edited" outline; the SYNC INVARIANT is preserved by never touching a note's `time`). Smart edit INVERTS this: the sheet must be authoritative AND mutated, so we need a persistent NOTATION model (measures, note-values, voices, accidentals, rests, ties) that does not exist yet. `VisNote[]` cannot be the edit model: shortening a note to "an eighth" has no representation there, and "this bar doesn't add up" is unanswerable without bar/meter structure.
  - **OSMD-as-editor: NOT viable. Verified against the installed package (opensheetmusicdisplay 1.9.9 under the main repo `node_modules`; note worktree package.json pins `^1.9.0`).** Concrete findings from the d.ts surface (`build/dist/src`): (1) NO MusicXML export anywhere. The only XML methods are `Mxl.MXLtoXMLstring` / `jszipToXMLstring` (decompress .mxl on import, INBOUND only). `osmd.exportSVG()` exports SVG, not notation. So an OSMD-internal edit can never round-trip back to MusicXML -> dead end for "sheet is source of truth". (2) The `Sheet`/`SourceMeasure` model HAS setters (`SourceMeasure.Duration`, `ActiveTimeSignature`, `VoiceEntry.Timestamp`, `Note.Length`) and notes expose `getAbsoluteTimestamp()` + `Length` (Fraction in whole-notes), so you COULD mutate it in place, but OSMD builds a SEPARATE `GraphicalSheet` from the source model and there is no public "re-layout after model mutation" path other than a full `osmd.render()`, and no serializer to persist the result. Mutating internal model objects is unsupported, undocumented, and version-fragile. (3) Hit-testing already works (proof: `src/sheet-overlay.ts:48` calls the undocumented `GraphicalNote.getSVGGElement()` and reads `getBoundingClientRect()` to place DOM labels), but that is READ-only notehead location, not a click->model-note edit handle. VERDICT: OSMD is a renderer, not an editor; "limited editing" is color/visibility only (confirmed by OSMD docs + the d.ts).
  - **Verovio IS the right substrate. Free: LGPLv3, OSI-approved (book.verovio.org/introduction/licensing). npm `verovio` (~29.5 MB install, WASM; ships `verovio/esm` + a separate wasm module; `@types/verovio` exists; runs in-browser). Hard "free tooling" rule satisfied.** The toolkit gives exactly the editor loop we need (from the toolkit-methods reference): `LoadData` (MusicXML in, auto-converts to MEI internally), `RenderToSVG` (render-from-model; MEI hierarchy is PRESERVED in the SVG so every notation element has a stable id in the DOM -> clean click hit-testing), `GetMEI` (round-trip OUT: full MEI, preserves un-edited beams/articulations/slurs/layout we are NOT editing in v1), and the SYNC primitives `GetElementsAtTime(ms)` + `GetTimeForElement(id)` (after `RenderToMIDI`) -> this is precisely how `stepTimes[]` / the time<->element map gets REBUILT from the edited model instead of hand-maintained. NOTE: Verovio's in-toolkit `Edit()`/`EditInfo()` are documented "experimental code not to rely on" - so do NOT drive edits through Verovio's editor; OWN the edit model in our code and treat Verovio purely as a deterministic render-from-model + sync-map engine.
  - **RECOMMENDED ARCHITECTURE (option (b) in the brief, sharpened): a small in-house editable notation model is the single source of truth.** Pipeline per edit: user gesture -> command mutates our notation model (measures/voices/note-values/accidentals/rests/ties) -> model serializes to MusicXML -> `verovio.loadData(xml)` + `renderToSVG()` (live staff re-render) -> walk the SAME model to rebuild `VisNote[]` + `stepTimes[]` + dispose/rebuild the Tone.js `Part` (reuse the existing narrow-rebuild path `reloadNotes` at `src/main.ts:343`, which already pauses/restores the transport so the swap is inaudible). The sync map is ALWAYS derived from the post-edit model (never hand-edited), so the sync invariant (falling notes + cursor share one timestamp source) holds by construction - same property `extractScore` relies on today. Rejected (a) "mutate the source MusicXML DOM + reload": tempting (no new model) but XML-DOM surgery for duration/rest/tie changes is brittle, has no clean undo, and still needs a notation model to validate "bar adds up". Rejected (c) "mutate OSMD's internal Sheet": no serializer, unsupported, version-fragile (see above).
  - **RENDERER DECISION: Verovio for the editor surface. Migration cost off OSMD is BOUNDED and need not be big-bang.** OSMD is currently load-bearing for: the highlight CURSOR (`osmd.cursor`), notehead positions for the label overlay (`sheet-overlay.ts`), and `extractScore` (reads `osmd.Sheet` + cursor iterator). Verovio replaces all three (SVG element ids for positions/click; `GetElementsAtTime` for the cursor; model-walk for extract). Phased: keep OSMD as the read-only viewer for un-edited scores, introduce Verovio ONLY inside edit mode behind a flag, then unify on Verovio once edit mode is solid. Two renderers can coexist briefly (only one renders the visible sheet at a time). Verovio's runtime cost is a multi-MB WASM payload: LAZY-load it on first entry to edit mode (mirror the existing Basic-Pitch lazy `import()` at `src/main.ts:498`), so non-editing users never pay it.
  - **HARD PARTS / TOP RISKS, ranked.** (1) DURATION/RHYTHM editing + re-deriving times and rebuilding the sync map - HIGHEST VALUE (project memory: geom OMR is prod-primary with duration_acc 0.0, so users WILL need to fix rhythm) and hardest. MuseScore fixed-bar model (shorten -> trailing rests, nothing after moves; show a "bar doesn't add up" meter-validation badge) is the right call; avoids text-reflow across barlines. Needs real measure/voice/tuplet-aware time math. (2) Re-render latency during a DRAG (pitch drag = many renders/sec). Verovio full-page re-render may be too slow for per-frame drag; mitigate by dragging a lightweight SVG ghost and only re-running loadData+render on DROP, re-rendering just the affected system/page where possible, and debouncing. MEASURE THIS EARLY (spike). (3) UNDO/REDO from day one: use a COMMAND stack (invertible edit ops) over our model, NOT XML/snapshot diffing (snapshots of MusicXML strings are simple but heavy and lose selection/caret context); the model is small enough that command-pattern inverses are clean and also give redo + edit coalescing (e.g. a drag = one undo step). Secondary risks: grand-staff + multi-voice correctness, and cross-staff (hand) moves = re-parenting a note between staves while keeping vertical position sane.
  - **STAGED BUILD PLAN (smallest shippable first; de-risk the unknowns earliest).** SPIKE-WITHIN-SPIKE (do before committing, ~1-2 days each): (S1) Verovio render+round-trip: load one of our OMR MusicXML outputs, `renderToSVG`, `getMEI`, reload it, confirm fidelity of beams/slurs we are NOT editing. (S2) Sync map: render a known score, build the time<->element map from `GetElementsAtTime`/`GetTimeForElement`, confirm it reproduces today's `stepTimes[]` within tolerance (proves the invariant survives the renderer swap). (S3) Drag-render latency: measure ms for loadData+render on a 1-2 page grand staff; decides whether drag needs the ghost/partial-render path. Then SHIP IN ORDER: P0 Verovio viewer parity (cursor + click-select) behind an edit-mode flag, no mutation yet (lowest risk, proves the substrate). P1 PITCH editing on the staff (move note up/down a line/space + toggle accidental), model + command-undo + full re-derive - this alone is high value given geom pitch is decent but not perfect, and it exercises the whole edit->render->re-derive->sync loop on the EASY axis before rhythm. P2 ADD/DELETE notes + rests. P3 DURATION editing with fixed-bar behavior + the "bar doesn't add up" validator (the hard, highest-value increment; gated on the S3 latency result). P4 cross-staff (hand) moves + multi-voice polish. Round-trip preservation of dynamics/slurs/ornaments/tuplets/repeats (OUT for v1 edits) is handled FREE by `GetMEI` as long as we never touch those subtrees.

- **2026-06-03 - RUNG 1 of our own OMR engine: GPU-FREE GEOMETRIC PITCH PIPELINE measured. `omr-worker/geom_omr.py` + `test_geom_omr.py`. Branch `feat/omr-geom-pitch`. HEADLINE: geometry SOLVES the LLM octave problem on clean input (synthetic octave-accuracy 0.972 vs the LLM's effective octave-weakness), but the CLASSICAL notehead/staff detector, not the decode, is the bottleneck on REAL scores.** RESEARCH ONLY (pure module, never wired into worker.process_job, mirrors reconcile-before-wired). Module: numpy/scipy/PIL, never-raises; `decode_pitch(y, staff_lines, clef)` is pure diatonic line/space counting from the clef bottom-line reference (treble bottom line=E4, bass=G2), `detect_systems` (every 5-line group via full-width-dark rows, soft 0.35*w threshold), `detect_noteheads` (staff-line removal + SMALL vertical close ~0.3 interline to NOT fuse stacked chord heads + tall-blob row-projection split to recover stacked heads + connected-components size/fill/aspect filter), `group_chords` (x-cluster within 1.2 interline), `transcribe_geometric` -> MusicXML via the tested `llm_omr.score_json_to_musicxml`. Tests (30, all pass on the cx33 scipy/PIL tier; 22 pure-tier pass anywhere incl. CI/local-no-scipy): the core test DRAWS synthetic staves with PIL and asserts decode_pitch returns the exact pitch+octave for treble AND bass at lines/spaces/ledgers, plus never-raise-on-garbage.
  - **MEASURED (cx33, Verovio-rendered clean synthetic, mean over 20 seeds, after detector fixes):** exact note-F1 **0.774**, pitch-class F1 0.796, **octave accuracy 0.972**, chord_recall ~0.01. Before the detector fixes (tighter staff threshold + vertical-close tuning + tall-blob splitting): exact-F1 0.551, octave 0.874, head recall ~80%. So the decode is essentially exact on clean input; the residual exact-F1 gap to the 0.90 baseline is almost entirely notehead-detection RECALL (pred 771 vs truth 836), not octave/pitch errors.
  - **MEASURED on REAL icarus.pdf vs icarus.mscz (mscx_to_truth_musicxml):** per-measure exact-F1 0.166 (hurt by no-barline bucketing). The honest GLOBAL (measure-agnostic) decomposition: pitch-CLASS recall **0.747** (= the LLM's 0.75: geometry reads note NAMES just as well), but exact-midi recall 0.411 and **octave accuracy only 0.55**. Detector found 119 of 146 noteheads (recall ~0.82, much better than the 48/146 before fixes).
  - **VERDICT vs the headline question "does geometry beat the LLM octave problem?":** YES on CLEAN renders (octave 0.97), NO YET on real scores (octave 0.55). The determinism is real but it rides on staff-line geometry + interline + ledger-count accuracy, which degrade on real input and throw notes a full octave off. Two named bottlenecks, both in the CLASSICAL detector (not the decode): (1) notehead RECALL on real scores, (2) octave robustness from noisy staff/ledger geometry on real scores. chord_recall ~0 even after splitting (stacked-head split helps detection but the chord-onset grouping still rarely reconstructs the exact pitch-set).
  - **RECOMMENDATION: a GPU-trained notehead/staff DETECTOR is the high-leverage next investment, NOT a learned pitch decoder.** The decode is already provably exact (0.97 octave on clean) - replacing it with ML would be wasted. The win is feeding the exact geometric decode with accurate notehead centers + staff geometry on real/photographed scores, which is exactly what a trained detector (e.g. a YOLO-style notehead+staffline model) provides. Cheaper non-GPU rungs to try first: robust interline/ledger estimation per-staff, deskew, barline detection (to fix the per-measure metric + chord onsets), and adaptive binarization for photos. Headline number to remember: **clean octave 0.972, real octave 0.55, real pitch-class 0.747.**

- **2026-06-03 - CODE REVIEW of `feat/omr-llm-transcriber` (PR #162): SHIP. Verdict: no blocking findings.** Reviewed `llm_omr.py` + worker wiring + tests against the never-raise / inert-by-default / PDF-fallback-safety contracts.
